               <div class="D-ib" style="height:40px;padding:0 11.5px;">
                <a class="D-ib" href="https://www.twitter.com/YahooTravel" rel="me" target="_blank">
                 <i class="Icon Fw-n Va-t" style="color:#00aceb;height:40px;line-height:40px;font-size:16px;">
                  
                 </i>
                </a>
                <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="content:;position:absolute;border-style:solid;border-top-width:0;border-bottom-width:8px;border-left-width:7px;border-right-width:7px;border-color:white transparent;display:block;height:0;width:0;z-index:2147483647;top:30px;left:50%;margin-left:-7px;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">
                </div>
                <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="content:;position:absolute;border-style:solid;border-top-width:0;border-bottom-width:9px;border-left-width:8px;border-right-width:8px;border-color:#e7e7e7 transparent;display:block;height:0;width:0;z-index:2147483646;top:29px;left:50%;margin-left:-8px;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">

                 <div style="position:relative;background-color:white;-webkit-border-radius:5px;-moz-border-radius:5px;-khtml-border-radius:5px;border-radius:5px;border:solid 1px #e7e7e7;padding:4px;z-index:2147483645;">

                </div>

                 <div style="position:relative;background-color:white;-webkit-border-radius:5px;-moz-border-radius:5px;-khtml-border-radius:5px;border-radius:5px;border:solid 1px #e7e7e7;padding:4px;z-index:2147483645;">

          <div class="Pos-r Z-0 article-container legacy" data-template="desktop" id="article-12-awe-inspiring-american-castles" style="background-color:white;min-height:315px;">
           <div class="Pos-r sticky-container print-article" style="min-height:315px;">
            <div class="article-inner-container" style="max-width:1280px;">
             <div class="inset-container Mx-a">
              <div class="GridTable">
               <div class="D-tbr row-template">
                <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left">
                 <div class="content" style="width:825px;min-width:825px;">
                  <noscript>
                  </noscript>
                  <noscript>
                  </noscript>
                  <div class="GridTable grid-content">
                   <div class="D-tbr row-content">
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left Pend-20" style="width:305px;max-width:305px;">
                     <h1 class="Font-A-6-110 title W-100" id="article-aft-title-12-awe-inspiring-american-castles">
                      10 awe-inspiring American castles
                     </h1>
                     <div class="attribution-component D-b W-100" id="article-aft-attribution-12-awe-inspiring-american-castles" style="max-width:305px;">
                      <div class="author-info author-info-text-first Pt-10 W-100 Bd-t Bd-b Bdstart-0 Bdend-0">
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t provider-info">
                          <a class="provider-logo" href="http://www.budgettravel.com/" target="_blank">
                           <img alt="Budget Travel" class="Maw-100" src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/YpTNl9D0GHlu2oczMJNEsA--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO2ZpPWZpdDt3PTE1MA--/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2011/10/21/provider-budgettravel_063012.png"/>
                          </a>
                          <div class="provider-alias C-n">
                           <a class="Font-C-2-140 Fw-b" href="http://www.budgettravel.com/" target="_blank">
                            Budget Travel
                           </a>
                          </div>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t">
                          <cite class="byline col D-b Fs-n" style="padding-bottom:15px;">
                           <span class="Font-C-2-140 Fw-n D-b">
                            Justin Ocean
                           </span>
                           <time class="date Font-C-2-140 Fw-n D-b">
                            <span>
                             August 16, 2012
                            </span>
                           </time>
                          </cite>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right" style="max-width:500px;">
                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-12-awe-inspiring-american-castles" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <div>
                          <div>
                           <img align="middle" alt="10 awe-inspiring American castles" class="editorial " src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/GE9LOT6d3Ufc5uyhr0WHpg--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9ODAw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/08/16/01-castello-di-amorosa-jpeg_000137.jpg" title="Castello di Amorosa (Photo: Brian Jannsen / AgeFotostock)" width="800"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            Castello di Amorosa (Photo: Brian Jannsen / AgeFotostock)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </div>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                         </span>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                         <div>
                          <h4 style="margin:3px 0px 8px 5px;padding:0px;font-size:10px;font-weight:bold;font-family:verdana;color:#555555;text-transform:uppercase;">
                           MORE AT BUDGET TRAVEL
                          </h4>
                          <ul style="margin:3px;padding:0px;list-style-type:none;font-family:verdana;font-size:10px;">
                           <li style="margin:0px 0px 6px 3px;padding:0px;list-style-type:none;list-style-position:inside;">
                            <em style="font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;color:#db612d;">
                             
                            </em>
                            <span class="Apple-converted-space">
                            </span>
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:b2eca691-359c-311a-a864-763d26043923;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.budgettravel.com/slideshow/budget-travel-advice-spy-gadgets-that-can-improve-your-vacation,8807" style="color:#1053fc;text-decoration:none;" target="_blank">
                             8 Spy Gadgets to Improve Your Vacation
                            </a>
                           </li>
                           <li style="margin:0px 0px 6px 3px;padding:0px;list-style-type:none;list-style-position:inside;">
                            <em style="font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;color:#db612d;">
                             
                            </em>
                            <span class="Apple-converted-space">
                            </span>
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:b2eca691-359c-311a-a864-763d26043923;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.budgettravel.com/slideshow/vacation-ideas-passport-stamps-worth-bragging-about,8884" style="color:#1053fc;text-decoration:none;" target="_blank">
                             Passport Stamps Worth Bragging About
                            </a>
                           </li>
                           <li style="margin:0px 0px 6px 3px;padding:0px;list-style-type:none;list-style-position:inside;">
                            <em style="font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;color:#db612d;">
                             
                            </em>
                            <span class="Apple-converted-space">
                            </span>
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:b2eca691-359c-311a-a864-763d26043923;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.budgettravel.com/slideshow/5-european-countries-where-prices-have-decreased-t,7685" style="color:#1053fc;text-decoration:none;" target="_blank">
                             5 European Countries Where Prices Have Decreased the Most
                            </a>
                           </li>
                          </ul>
                         </div>
                         <span>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          Who doesn't go a bit giddy at the sight of a castle? The good news is that you don't have to head to Europe for honest-to-goodness ones of the Cinderella varietywe have plenty right here in our own backyard. Railroad barons commissioned most of these estates, but at least one housed a legitimate king and queen (bet you didn't know this country had its own history of royalty!). Each is an engineering wonder in its own right, with some even constructed out of old-world castles that were shipped across the ocean. And each is open to tours should you decide to make a trip (a select few will even let you spend the night). Read this and you might just discover a side of America you never knew existed.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <strong>
                          Castello di Amorosa
                         </strong>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          Word to the wise: Imbibe the cabernet sauvignon and pinot grigio at the Castello di Amorosa winery carefully, because somewhere in the 121,000-square-foot, 107-room, eight-level complex there's a dungeon with a functional Renaissance-era iron maiden. It took 14 years to construct the castle using historically accurate medieval building techniques. The end result is an "authentic" 12th- and 13th-century Tuscan castle with drawbridge and moat. The frescoes in the Great Hall and Knights' Chamber are hand-painted, some 8,000 tons of Napa Valley stone hand-chiseled, the Hapsburg-era bricks, hand-forged nails and chandeliers, and 500-year-old fireplace all tediously imported from Europe. That sense of awe? Very modern. 4045 N. St. Helena Highway,
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-474147-calistoga_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Calistoga, CA
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          , 707/967-6272, castellodiamorosa.com. Admission $18, including wine tasting.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/danjaiQ.XkXPOm762Mja4g--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/08/16/02-hearst-jpg_000137.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="Hearst Castle (Photo: Stock Connection / SuperStock)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            Hearst Castle (Photo: Stock Connection / SuperStock)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <strong>
                          Hearst Castle
                         </strong>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          Understatement of the millennium: William Randolph Hearst's 1919 directive to architect Julia Morgan to "build a little something" on his ranch in San Simeon. Then again, a 115-room "Casa Grande" inspired by a Spanish cathedral is a relatively modest proposition compared to the 250,000 acres and the 13 miles of coastline it's set on. It's when you add in the three additional Mediterranean Revival guesthouses (46 more rooms total), 127 acres of gardens, the Neptune pool with authentic Roman temple pediment, the zoo with roaming reindeer and zebra, Egyptian Sekhmet statues on the terraces, and the private airstrip that things get a bit over-the-top. Magnificent doesn't begin to describe the museum-quality artwork, which drove the architecture as much as anything, from Renaissance statuary to Gothic tapestries and entire ceilings, nor the palatial scale of the publishing magnate's vision for "La Cuesta Encantada" (The Enchanted Hill)still unfinished upon his death in 1951. 750 Hearst Castle Rd., San Simeon,
                         </span>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:0;max-width:500px;">
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-191501880-california_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           CA
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          , 800/444-4445, hearstcastle.org. Admission from $25.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/eAssPFXiqScR8yJQp6C28g--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/08/16/03-bishopspalaceexterior-7262012-17132-horiz-large-jpeg_000137.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="Bishop's Palace (Photo: Galveston Historical Foundation / David Canright)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            Bishop's Palace (Photo: Galveston Historical Foundation / David Canright)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <strong>
                          Bishop's Palace
                         </strong>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          Of all the Gilded Age Victorians built by Nicholas Clayton along Galveston's Gulf Coast, the Bishop's Palace (ne Gresham Castle, 1893, after its original owner, Santa Fe railroad magnate Walther Gresham) remains the grandestand not just because its steel and stone hulk survived the Great Storm of 1900. Its small lot and oversized proportions with chteau-esque detailing of steeply peaked rooflines and sculptural chimneys still dominate the street, while inside the 14-foot coffered ceilings, 40-foot octagonal mahogany stairwell, stained glass, plaster carvings, and Sienna marble columns exude richness. Keep a lookout for the bronze dragon sculptures. After serving as a Catholic bishop's residence for 50 years, the house is now open for tours. Book a private guide to see the usually off-limits third floor. 1402 Broadway,
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-479594-galveston_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Galveston, TX
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          , 409/762-2475, galveston.com. Admission $10, private tours from $50.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/10ywCUPenabX.stbFqeiEQ--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/08/16/04-boldtexterior-7262012-164445-horiz-large-jpeg_000137.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="Boldt Castle (Photo: Boldt Castle)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            Boldt Castle (Photo: Boldt Castle)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <strong>
                          Boldt Castle
                         </strong>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          What do you do when you come across a heart-shaped isle while vacationing with your wife in the Thousand Islands? If you're upstart industrialist George Boldt, you buy it and hire 300 stonemasons, carpenters, and artists to build a six-story, 120-room testament to your love. There were Italian gardens, a dove-cote, and a turreted powerhouse, plus all the imported Italian marble, French silks, and Oriental rugs money could buy. But when his wife Louise died in 1904, the heartbroken Boldt ceased construction on the Rhineland-style Taj Mahal and left it to the elements for 73 years. Today, tourists can visit from May to October for self-guided toursor book a wedding in the stone gazebo. +44 20' 40.29" N, -75 55' 21.27" W, Heart Island,
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-477852-alexandria_bay_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Alexandria Bay
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          , NY, 315/482-9724, boldtcastle.com. Admission $8.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/G5Yv0ZtSCORhHR3x_ZBEBg--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/08/16/05-castlescastleinthecloudsinterior-jpeg_000137.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="Castle in the Clouds (Photo: Castle in the Clouds)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            Castle in the Clouds (Photo: Castle in the Clouds)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <strong>
                          Castle in the Clouds
                         </strong>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          Location, location, locationas important in castles to fending off conquers as forgetting Gilded Age woes. And for millionaire shoe baron Thomas Plant, that meant setting his 1914 Lucknow Estate (named after the Indian city he loved) on the rim of an extinct caldera high in the Ossipee Mountains with unbroken views over 6,300 private acres of woods and lakes. The mansion by comparison is relatively subdued: A mere 16 rooms, it's practically minuscule compared to the other castles on this list. Throughout, the arts and crafts philosophy of artisanship and living in harmony with nature is expressed in the stone walls, inventive handiwork like the jigsaw floor in the kitchen, and functional decor that eschews ostentationall planned at Plant's 5-foot-4 heightplus a few technological innovations like a needle shower, self-cleaning oven, brine fridge, and central-vacuuming system. Much remains wholly preserved today. Route 171, 455 Old Mountain Rd.,
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-24891419-moultonborough_nh_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Moultonborough, NH
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          , 603/476-5900, castleintheclouds.org. Admission $16.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/2.fuYI8gNUrvGTkMISQvWA--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/08/16/06-greytowerscastle-jpeg_000141.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="Grey Towers Castle (Photo: Ike9898/Wikimedia Commons)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            Grey Towers Castle (Photo: Ike9898/Wikimedia Commons)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <strong>
                          Grey Towers Castle
                         </strong>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          Most colleges contend to be fortresses of learning, but Arcadia University in the suburbs north of Philadelphia can back it up with battlements acquired in 1929. Grey Towers was built by eclectic sugar refiner William Welsh Harrison between 1893 and 1898 and modeled after Northumberland's Alnwick Castle (a.k.a. the most archetypal expression of the medieval style). The 40 rooms wowed with gilded ceilings, tapestries, ornamental paintings, and hand-carved walnut and mahogany woodwork in styles from French Renaissance to Louis XVand of course a Mirror Roomwhile secret passages behind fireplaces and underground tunnels. Self-guided tours of public areas are possible while classes are in session (the building now contains dorm rooms and administration offices). Free brochures outline the history. 450 South Easton Rd., Glenside,
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://Glenside,%20PA" target="_blank">
                           PA
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          , 215/572-2900, arcadia.edu.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/UpZ3pHgSZGmICwiWmMLPXg--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/08/16/07-iolaniexterior-7262012-15534-horiz-large-jpeg_000142.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="'Iolani (Photo: Jiang/Wikimedia Commons)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            'Iolani (Photo: Jiang/Wikimedia Commons)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <strong>
                          'Iolani Palace
                         </strong>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          Other properties on this list may be bigger and more lavish, but the 'Iolani Palace has one thing above them all: legitimacy. America's only true palaceas in, royalty resided herewas built from 1879 to 1882 by King Kalakua and Queen Kapi'olani. The goal was to enhance the prestige of modern Hawaii in a kind of Victorian-era keeping up with the Joneses. (The palace had electricity and a telephone even before the White House.) Stone-faced with plenty of koa wood inside, the two-floor American Florentinestyle building includes a throne room, grand hall, and private suites, including the upstairs room where the queen was imprisoned for five months following the 1895 coup. Today, concerted efforts are underway to find artifacts and furniture (like the king's ebony and gilt bedroom set) that were auctioned off by the post-coup Provisional Government. 364 South King St.,
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-191501917-honolulu_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Honolulu, HI
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          , 808/522-0832, iolanipalace.org. Admission $12, guided tour $20.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/vDLLB7.rvpxPQX7L6ykNOw--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/08/16/08-fonthillexterior-7262012-163622-horiz-large-jpeg_000142.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="Fonthill (Photo: 2daysphotos.com)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            Fonthill (Photo: 2daysphotos.com)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <strong>
                          Fonthill Castle
                         </strong>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          Celebrating its centennial in 2012, the former home of industrialist-turned-archaeologist Henry Mercer is an ode to artisanship: All 44 rooms (10 bathrooms, five bedrooms, and 200 windows), 32 stairwells, 18 fireplaces, and 21 chimneys are hewn from hand-mixed reinforced concrete in a mishmash of medieval, Gothic, and Byzantine styles. Thousands of handcrafted ceramic tiles were inset throughout, including Mercer's own Moravian-style tiles plus Persian, Chinese, Spanish, and Dutch productions he collected. Today, the 60-acre Bucks County estate serves as a museum to pre-industrial life, with 900 American and European prints at Fonthill and even more artifacts (like a whale boat and Conestoga wagon) in its sister building, the Mercer Museum, a fun houselike six-story castle in its own right. East Court St. and Rt. 313,
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-478948-doylestown_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Doylestown, PA
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          , 215/348-9461, mercermuseum.org. Admission $12
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/eq9AEd4kkRJhZ9o1f8J4CQ--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/08/16/09-giletteexterior-jpeg_000143.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="Gillette Castle (Photo: Rootology/Wikimedia Commons)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            Gillette Castle (Photo: Rootology/Wikimedia Commons)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <strong>
                          Gillette Castle
                         </strong>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          It's elementary: Get famous (and rich) by playing Sherlock Holmes on the stage; build your own Baskerville Hall. Pet project of campy eccentric William Hooker Gillette, the 24-room castle was completed in 1919 by a crew of 20 men over five years using the actor/playwright's own drafts and designs. It's also the focal point of his 184-acre Seventh Sister estate, a forested bluff overlooking the Connecticut River. Outside, the local fieldstone reads like crumbling medieval; inside, the built-in couches, curious detailing, and inventive hand-carved southern white oak woodwork is all arts and crafts. As for cat images? There are 60. (Gillette had 17 feline friends.) Gillette Castle State Park, 67 River Rd., East Haddam,
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-191501900-connecticut_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           CT
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          , 860/526-2336, ct.gov. Grounds open year-round; interior tours available Memorial Day to Columbus Day. Admission $6.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/y.gNt2ePLxIwkrervflR6Q--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/08/16/10-ohekaexterior-7272012-12319-horiz-large-jpeg_000143.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="OHEKA Castle (Photo: Oheka Castle)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            OHEKA Castle (Photo: Oheka Castle)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <strong>
                          OHEKA Castle
                         </strong>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          Second behind Asheville's Biltmore as the largest private estate in the nation, OHEKAan acronym of Otto Herman Kahn, its millionaire financier original ownerended up abandoned in the late 1970s and sustained extensive damage from fires, vandals, and neglect. After a 20-year renovation, it's back in form and is now a 32-room luxury hotel. Think Downton Abbey just an hour from Manhattan (themed packages available), or for that matter, Citizen Kane (photos of it were used in the film). Originally set on 443 acres, massive tons of earth were moved to make the hilltop location of the 127-room, 109,000-square-foot manse the highest point in Long Island. The Olmsted Brothers planned the formal gardens, the Grand Staircase was inspired by Fontainebleau's famous exterior one, and 126 servants tended to the six-person family when they came for weekends and summers. The 1919 price tag: $11 million. That's $110 million in today's money. Sounds about right for a man whose likeness inspired Mr. Monopoly. 135 West Gate Dr.,
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-4957035-huntington_ny_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Huntington, NY
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          , 631/659-1400, oheka.com. Admission $25. Double rooms from $395 per night. Guided tours available.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://www.budgettravel.com/slideshow/photos-12-amazing-american-castles,8851" target="_blank">
                           See more awe-inspiring American castles
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                        </div>

                       <div class="item-tag Tt-u Font-C-1-115 Fw-b" style="margin-left:175px;">
                        <a class="tag" data-action-outcome="navigate" data-ylk="g:a1325855-3a7f-321b-8871-81f828617ea2;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:also;ad:0;cpos:2;itc:0;t9:48;elm:itm;elmt:cat" href="/travel/tagged/biz-travel" style="color:#999;">
                         Biz Travel
                        </a>
                       </div>
                       <a data-action-outcome="open" data-routable-url="/travel/1/traveling-with-your-boss-heres-how-not-to-make-123738714629.html" data-ylk="g:a1325855-3a7f-321b-8871-81f828617ea2;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:also;ad:0;cpos:2;itc:0;t8:tileview;t9:21;elm:img;elmt:ct;" href="/travel/traveling-with-your-boss-heres-how-not-to-make-123738714629.html" style="color:#000;">
                        <span class="item-title Font-A-3-120 D-b" style="word-wrap:break-word;margin-left:175px;">
                         Traveling With Your Boss? HeresHow Not to Make a Fool of Yourself
                        </span>

The Walt Disney Co. is getting the break because they intend to spend the money on a $1 billion expansion of their parks in Anaheim. This makeover will not only lead to new attractions, it will also mean more jobs for the people of Anaheim.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDisney is already the biggest employer in the city, providing 28,000 jobs for those in surrounding communities. HeresHow Not to Make a Fool of Yourself","summary":"If you want to keep your job, we suggest you read on and take notes.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F0a81f1e965a02fa22fbf86c49f5e4d56427af105.gif\" alt=\"Traveling With Your Boss? Here&#x2019;s&#xA0;How Not to Make a Fool of Yourself\" width=\"540\" height=\"766\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EIllustration by Erik Mace\u002FYahoo\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThere&#x2019;s a business trip on the calendar, and you&#x2019;re traveling with your boss. While it might seem like common sense, there are some very simple dos and don&#x2019;ts of to remember when you&#x2019;re traveling with your superior. If you want to keep your job, we suggest you read on and take notes.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EDon&#x2019;t pack like you&#x2019;re going on vacation\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F3660b6618760b55cfb20418ee69c36ca9f38b71b.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EAppropriately dressed woman on work trip. &#xA0;(Photo: Thinkstock)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ETranslation: Leave the Herve Leger dresses, short shorts, and sheer blouses at home. Regardless of where your work trip takes you&#x2014;New York City, Jamaica or Miami&#x2014; this is not the time to show some skin, bare your cleavage or prove just how toned SoulCycle has made your legs. The rule is simple: If you wouldn&#x2019;t wear it to work, don&#x2019;t wear it on a work trip. Office-appropriate dress codes still apply. Should your job take you somewhere warm (who among us has been able to avoid the Las Vegas Convention Center), make sure to pack light fabrics that breathe as opposed to slinky ones that make others breathe heavy&#x2014;it&#x2019;s an important differentiation.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftravel\u002Ftake-a-bizcation-96120868057.html\"\u003EThe Bizcation: The Ultimate Way to Enjoy Business Travel\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EJust say no to the in-flight service-slash-mini bar-slash-lobby bar\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fb8a8ff8c2d10d4a58a3309b0a82d2e594e48e27a.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ETiny liquor bottles on ice (Photo: Thinkstock)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWe get it, the jingle of tiny bottles on the flight attendant&#x2019;s cart as it passes by you on a long plane trip is tempting. Or the way the miniature versions of your favorite liquor are arranged so beautifully in your room&#x2019;s mini bar. Or how that beautiful, deep mahogany lobby bar seems to be calling your name, asking you to sit down and stay a while. Just. Say. No.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EGetting drunk or even buzzed can lead to awkward moments when spending off-duty hours with your boss. This is not the time to get sloppy and explain to him\u002Fher that you really do deserve that promotion\u002Fraise\u002Fcorner office. That&#x2019;s not to say you can&#x2019;t have a drink with dinner&#x2014;being a straightedge isn&#x2019;t necessarily good either&#x2014;but know your limit and stay South of it. Like Deep South of it. &#xA0; \u003Cb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EKeep the conversation topics bland and water-cooler appropriate.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"355\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fd0815c7beea6506bea9ca3a34c162c583753a6d0.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EKeep conversation work friendly (Photo: Thinkstock)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI&#x2019;m sorry you&#x2019;re getting divorced, but just because we boarded a plane together doesn&#x2019;t mean I want to hear about it. This is not the time to bare your soul to your boss. If you wouldn&#x2019;t casually say it while small talking in the office hallway then don&#x2019;t say it now. &#xA0;It may \u003Ci\u003Efeel\u003C\u002Fi\u003E like personal time given that you are out of the office&#x2014;perhaps spending a lot of time together in the airport or hotel&#x2014;but that doesn&#x2019;t mean confessing all your private affairs is a good idea. Your boss likely does not want to hear about your ne&#x2019;er-do-well brother, complicated finances, weird rash, nasty divorce, or last Tinder date. Not only does it cross into some uncomfortable gray area, it could perhaps work against you later should they be one of the loose-lipped variety. Keep your personal business just that&#x2014;personal.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EStop calling\u002Ftexting your significant other\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"380\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F0ef53769808b0859321453009d2426f84bf47fa1.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EKeep texts to your &#xA0;girlfriend\u002Fboyfriend\u002Fhusband\u002Fwife to a minimum (Photo: ThinkStock)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EYou&#x2019;re on a work trip and miss your girlfriend\u002Fboyfriend\u002Fhusband\u002Fwife. That does not give you permission to spend half the trip on your phone, texting flirty messages, endless emojis, and selfie after selfie of you in front of the [fill in recognizable landmark here]. Check in with him\u002Fher from the privacy of your own hotel room at the beginning of the day and again at the end if necessary. Constant communication&#x2014;especially during a meeting or lecture&#x2014;is unprofessional, not to mention annoying for those around you. Your relationship should be able to withstand a few days apart. Remember, absence is supposed to make the heart grow fonder, not make you go over your data plan.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThis is a work trip, not a dating app\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F4f162efe5e6aafac08acf3f527e7536a8c700323.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EStop flirting with the waiter\u002Fconcierge\u002Fguy at bar or&#x2014;gasp&#x2014;coworker.&#xA0;(Photo: Thickstock)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESure, you&#x2019;re away from home and meeting new people you may or may not find attractive. Or perhaps you never noticed just how cute your coworker is (and he\u002Fshe is funny! Who knew?), but still, out-and-out flirting is a bad idea that can get you into trouble and send a message about you that you don&#x2019;t want communicated. Keep things rated G to avoid a bad rating from your higher-ups.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftravel\u002Fhotels-are-courting-a-new-generation-of-business-101706056027.html\"\u003EHotels Are Courting a New Generation of Business Travelers\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EGo on a social media diet\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fda0a1d90752391607c29d9763173282b11c78cc6.jpg\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EA work trip is not the time for revealing selfies. (Photo: Thickstock)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ESo you&#x2019;re keeping it together during your meetings\u002Fwork meals but the second you leave your boss&#x2019; sight, you post a selfie on Instagram.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#xA0;Photo: You in front of the mirror in your hotel room. Caption: &#x201C;Ugh, work trips are such a drag!&#x201D; &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EYour boss may or may not follow you, but if you have a non-private account he or she likely looks at your posts from time to time. Remember that before hitting &#x201C;share.&#x201D; Do yourself a favor and use the few days away to take a break from social media. (Photo: Thinkstock)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAirports are going to pot.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPassengers traveling on flights within Oregon will be allowed to transport a small amount of weed, after the state&#x2019;s recreational marijuana law went into effect July 1.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAccording to \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.kptv.com\u002Fstory\u002F29506836\u002Fportland-international-airport-changes-recreational-pot-policy#ixzz3fVHH2LFg\"\u003EFox 12 Oregon\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, people flying through Portland International Airport, Oregon&#x2019;s biggest airport, won&#x2019;t be dragged from the line and hauled away if security officials spot pot.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe Transportation Security Administration said its primary focus was to &#x201C;detect threats to aviation security,&#x201D; not stop adult marijuana users who obey the state&#x2019;s 1 ounce marijuana limit,\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.ibtimes.com\u002Fmarijuana-legalization-oregon-portland-airport-allows-travelers-bring-weed-state-2003572\"\u003E the International Business Times\u003C\u002Fa\u003E reported.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf a passenger is found carrying pot, security agents will alert airport police, who will investigate whether the traveler is of legal age to possess the marijuana and that they are not flying out of state.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPassengers traveling out of state will have to leave pot behind because transporting it to another place is still a federal offense.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I don&#x2019;t care if they got it in their pocket. I could care less as long as they can&#x2019;t smoke it in the airport, you can&#x2019;t smoke it in the airplane. So depends if wherever they&#x2019;re going if it&#x2019;s legal, that&#x2019;s fine with me,&#x201D; Arnold Lucht told Fox 12.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I&#x2019;m not anti-marijuana, but I&#x2019;m pro-hairspray. I would really like to have some hairspray or some shampoo. What&#x2019;s shampoo going to do to somebody? Why can&#x2019;t I take my shampoo on a plane? I think it&#x2019;s a little lopsided. Silly, it&#x2019;s actually silly,&#x201D; said Verena Douglas, who moved to Oregon from Colorado.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe news comes as recreational pot became legal in Oregon on July 1, a move celebrated on July 3 as hundreds of people gathered in downtown Portland for a &#x201C;Weed the People&#x201D; rally.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe State House has passed a bill allowing retail marijuana sales to begin on October 1.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe bill would allow tax-free retail sales through existing medical marijuana (AP Photo\u002FAlvaro Barrientos)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPAMPLONA, Spain (AP) - Two Spaniards were gored in the penultimate running of the bulls of Pamplona&#x2019;s San Fermin festival Monday, organizers said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe San Fermin press office said one was gored in the abdomen and another in the leg. A third Spaniard suffered knee bruises. None was reported to be in serious condition.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe June 6-14 fiesta, held annually to honor the northern city&#x2019;s patron saint, dates back to the late 16th century. It became world-famous after Ernest Hemingway featured it in his 1926 novel &#x201C;The Sun Also Rises&#x201D; and attracts thousands of tourists.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETen people, including four Americans, have been gored in this year&#x2019;s festival.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe daily run see thousands of people racing six fighting bulls along a narrow 930-yard (850-meter) course from a holding pen to the city&#x2019;s bullring. Monday&#x2019;s dash lasted 2 minutes, 12 seconds.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe bulls are killed by professional matadors in bullfights each afternoon during the festival.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBull runs are a traditional part of summer festivals across Spain. Greenlands Finest Microbrew Beers","summary":"I'm a beer woman. So on my trip to Greenland, when I heard there was a craft brewery in town, I made a beeline for it.","body":"\u003Cp\u003EAnybody who knows me knows I don&#x2019;t drink vodka. I don&#x2019;t do tequila. And I&#x2019;ve never been a big fan of anything that comes with a garnish. I am, however, a beer girl. Raised in Cincinnati, a town with German roots, I have a deep love of hops, and over the years my tastes have been refined from \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhudepohlbeer.com\u002F\"\u003EHudepohl\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and Schlitz to craft beers. Don&#x2019;t get me wrong &#x2014; when stuck on a riverboat for a bachelorette party in, say, Austin, Texas (thanks to my sister Emily), I will still happily down a Bud, a Coors, or a Schlitz. But I have learned to appreciate the fine craft of beer making and love a small-batch brew. So on my trip to Greenland, when I heard there was a craft brewery in town, I made a beeline for it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftravel\u002Ffinger-pulling-head-pulling-and-kick-the-seal-122521580652.html\"\u003EFinger Pulling and Kick the Seal &#x2014; Welcome to the Arctic Games!\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F93fb6d09ed4cf36c50b1cd8100b9a9da95be5f9d.png\" alt=\"Taste-Testing Greenland&#x2019;s Finest Microbrew Beers\" width=\"540\" height=\"304\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe Godthaab Bryghus brewery is in a building that conveniently also houses a dive bar called Daddy&#x2019;s. While &#x201C;Daddy&#x201D; is a great guy named Gert, the actual brewery is run by Mikael Sorenson, who swears that the beer there is made with glacier ice that is at least 2,000 years old.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Yes, we have men who go out onto the ice and cut slabs off the glaciers for us and bring them back here for our beer,&#x201D; Sorenson said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E[Side note: Apparently ice cutting is a big business. Down the street is an ice cream shop that also uses 2,000-year-old ice. &#x201C;Ice cream in Greenland?&#x201D; you may be asking. &#x201C;Isn&#x2019;t it cold enough?&#x201D; No. It&#x2019;s not. Greenland has the second largest ice cream consumption per capita in the world, second only to Finland. Go figure.]\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"304\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F3a590de53797cb2f646953e3212a190735cb2dff.png\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhile there are no official stats on how much beer is consumed in &#xA0;Nuuk, Greenland&#x2019;s capital, judging by the crowds in the bars and the continual snow, I&#x2019;d say it ranks right up there. And frankly, I can&#x2019;t say I blame them &#x2014; the weather is rough (see previous episode: &#x201C;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftravel\u002Fsnowmageddon-2015-cabin-fever-hits-hard-in-123462240287.html\"\u003ESnowmageddon 2015: Cabin Fever Hits Hard in Greenland\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x201D;), and the beer is delicious. At the time I visited, there were five beers on tap, including the Musk Ox, the Eric the Red, and the Polar Bear (they like to name the beers after local animals). And here&#x2019;s a tip: While they are all delicious, if you ever find yourself at Daddy&#x2019;s in Nuuk, ask for Gert and Mikael and get them to give you the unfiltered versions of all the beers. They may smell like dirty feet, but they taste like heaven.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftravel\u002Fsnowmageddon-2015-cabin-fever-hits-hard-in-123462240287.html\"\u003ESnowmageddon 2015: Cabin Fever Hits Hard in Greenland\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThere is only one problem with the Godthaab Bryghus beer &#x2014; while it is possibly the best beer I have ever tasted (and trust: I have tasted a lot of beer), they don&#x2019;t export. So to get 2,000-year-old glacier-water beer, you have to go to the source. It&#x2019;s worth it. \u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cb\u003ELet Yahoo Travel inspire you every day. \u003C\u002Ful\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n\u003Cspan style=\"color:#000000;font-family:&apos;Times New doesn&apos;t go a bit giddy at the sight of a castle? The good news is that you don&apos;t have to head to Europe for honest-to-goodness ones of the Cinderella variety&#x2014;we have plenty right here in our own backyard. Railroad barons commissioned most of these estates, but at least one housed a legitimate king and queen (bet you didn&apos;t know this country had its own history of royalty!). Each is an engineering wonder in its own right, with some even constructed out of old-world castles that were shipped across the ocean. And each is open to tours should you decide to make a trip (a select few will even let you spend the night). Read this and you might just discover a side of America you never knew existed.\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003ECastello di Amorosa\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003EWord to the wise: Imbibe the cabernet sauvignon and pinot grigio at the Castello di Amorosa winery carefully, because somewhere in the 121,000-square-foot, 107-room, eight-level complex there&apos;s a dungeon with a functional Renaissance-era iron maiden. It took 14 years to construct the castle using historically accurate medieval building techniques. The end result is an &quot;authentic&quot; 12th- and 13th-century Tuscan castle with drawbridge and moat. The frescoes in the Great Hall and Knights&apos; Chamber are hand-painted, some 8,000 tons of Napa Valley stone hand-chiseled, the Hapsburg-era bricks, hand-forged nails and chandeliers, and 500-year-old fireplace all tediously imported from Europe. That sense of awe? Very modern. 4045 N. Then again, a 115-room &quot;Casa Grande&quot; inspired by a Spanish cathedral is a relatively modest proposition compared to the 250,000 acres and the 13 miles of coastline it&apos;s set on. It&apos;s when you add in the three additional Mediterranean Revival guesthouses (46 more rooms total), 127 acres of gardens, the Neptune pool with authentic Roman temple pediment, the zoo with roaming reindeer and zebra, Egyptian Sekhmet statues on the terraces, and the private airstrip that things get a bit over-the-top. Magnificent doesn&apos;t begin to describe the museum-quality artwork, which drove the architecture as much as anything, from Renaissance statuary to Gothic tapestries and entire ceilings, nor the palatial scale of the publishing magnate&apos;s vision for &quot;La Cuesta Encantada&quot; (The Enchanted Hill)&#x2014;still unfinished upon his death in 1951. 750 Hearst Castle Rd., San Simeon, \n\u003Ca target=\"_blank\" href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftravel.yahoo.com\u002Fp-travelguide-191501880-california_vacations-i\"\u003ECA\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, 800\u002F444-4445, hearstcastle.org. Admission from $25.\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cspan class=\"yui-editorial-embed\"\u003E\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003Cimg title=\"Bishop&apos;s Palace (Photo: Galveston Historical Foundation \u002F David Canright)\" alt=\"\" class=\"editorial \" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" align=\"right\" width=\"320\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Flo\u002Fapi\u002Fres\u002F1.2\u002FeAssPFXiqScR8yJQp6C28g--\u002FYXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw\u002Fhttps:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fos\u002F153\u002F2012\u002F08\u002F16\u002F03-bishopspalaceexterior-7262012-17132-horiz-large-jpeg_000137.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cp class=\"legend\"\u003EBishop&apos;s Palace (Photo: Galveston Historical Foundation \u002F David Canright)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EBishop&apos;s Palace\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003EOf all the Gilded Age Victorians built by Nicholas Clayton along Galveston&apos;s Gulf Coast, the Bishop&apos;s Palace (n&#xE9;e Gresham Castle, 1893, after its original owner, Santa Fe railroad magnate Walther Gresham) remains the grandest&#x2014;and not just because its steel and stone hulk survived the Great Storm of 1900. Its small lot and oversized proportions with ch&#xE2;teau-esque detailing of steeply peaked rooflines and sculptural chimneys still dominate the street, while inside the 14-foot coffered ceilings, 40-foot octagonal mahogany stairwell, stained glass, plaster carvings, and Sienna marble columns exude richness. Keep a lookout for the bronze dragon sculptures. After serving as a Catholic bishop&apos;s residence for 50 years, the house is now open for tours. Admission $10, private tours from $50.\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cspan class=\"yui-editorial-embed\"\u003E\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003Cimg title=\"Boldt Castle (Photo: Boldt Castle)\" alt=\"\" class=\"editorial \" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" align=\"right\" width=\"320\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Flo\u002Fapi\u002Fres\u002F1.2\u002F10ywCUPenabX.stbFqeiEQ--\u002FYXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw\u002Fhttps:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fos\u002F153\u002F2012\u002F08\u002F16\u002F04-boldtexterior-7262012-164445-horiz-large-jpeg_000137.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cp class=\"legend\"\u003EBoldt Castle (Photo: Boldt Castle)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EBoldt Castle\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003EWhat do you do when you come across a heart-shaped isle while vacationing with your wife in the Thousand Islands? If you&apos;re upstart industrialist George Boldt, you buy it and hire 300 stonemasons, carpenters, and artists to build a six-story, 120-room testament to your love. There were Italian gardens, a dove-cote, and a turreted powerhouse, plus all the imported Italian marble, French silks, and Oriental rugs money could buy. But when his wife Louise died in 1904, the heartbroken Boldt ceased construction on the Rhineland-style Taj Mahal and left it to the elements for 73 years. Today, tourists can visit from May to October for self-guided tours&#x2014;or book a wedding in the stone gazebo. +44&#xB0; 20&apos; 40.29&quot; N, -75&#xB0; 55&apos; 21.27&quot; W, Heart Island, \n\u003Ca target=\"_blank\" href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftravel.yahoo.com\u002Fp-travelguide-477852-alexandria_bay_vacations-i\"\u003EAlexandria Bay\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, NY, 315\u002F482-9724, boldtcastle.com. Admission $8.\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cspan class=\"yui-editorial-embed\"\u003E\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003Cimg title=\"Castle in the Clouds (Photo: Castle in the Clouds)\" alt=\"\" class=\"editorial \" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" align=\"right\" width=\"320\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Flo\u002Fapi\u002Fres\u002F1.2\u002FG5Yv0ZtSCORhHR3x_ZBEBg--\u002FYXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw\u002Fhttps:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fos\u002F153\u002F2012\u002F08\u002F16\u002F05-castlescastleinthecloudsinterior-jpeg_000137.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cp class=\"legend\"\u003ECastle in the Clouds (Photo: Castle in the Clouds)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003ECastle in the Clouds\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003ELocation, location, location&#x2014;as important in castles to fending off conquers as forgetting Gilded Age woes. And for millionaire shoe baron Thomas Plant, that meant setting his 1914 Lucknow Estate (named after the Indian city he loved) on the rim of an extinct caldera high in the Ossipee Mountains with unbroken views over 6,300 private acres of woods and lakes. The mansion by comparison is relatively subdued: A mere 16 rooms, it&apos;s practically minuscule compared to the other castles on this list. Throughout, the arts and crafts philosophy of artisanship and living in harmony with nature is expressed in the stone walls, inventive handiwork like the jigsaw floor in the kitchen, and functional decor that eschews ostentation&#x2014;all planned at Plant&apos;s 5-foot-4 height&#x2014;plus a few technological innovations like a needle shower, self-cleaning oven, brine fridge, and central-vacuuming system. Much remains wholly preserved today. Admission $16.\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cspan class=\"yui-editorial-embed\"\u003E\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003Cimg title=\"Grey Towers Castle (Photo: Ike9898\u002FWikimedia Commons)\" alt=\"\" class=\"editorial \" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" align=\"right\" width=\"320\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Flo\u002Fapi\u002Fres\u002F1.2\u002F2.fuYI8gNUrvGTkMISQvWA--\u002FYXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw\u002Fhttps:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fos\u002F153\u002F2012\u002F08\u002F16\u002F06-greytowerscastle-jpeg_000141.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cp class=\"legend\"\u003EGrey Towers Castle (Photo: Ike9898\u002FWikimedia Commons)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EGrey Towers Castle\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003EMost colleges contend to be fortresses of learning, but Arcadia University in the suburbs north of Philadelphia can back it up with battlements acquired in 1929. Grey Towers was built by eclectic sugar refiner William Welsh Harrison between 1893 and 1898 and modeled after Northumberland&apos;s Alnwick Castle (a.k.a. the most archetypal expression of the medieval style). The 40 rooms wowed with gilded ceilings, tapestries, ornamental paintings, and hand-carved walnut and mahogany woodwork in styles from French Renaissance to Louis XV&#x2014;and of course a Mirror Room&#x2014;while secret passages behind fireplaces and underground tunnels. Self-guided tours of public areas are possible while classes are in session (the building now contains dorm rooms and administration offices). Free brochures outline the history. 450 South Easton Rd., Glenside, \n\u003Ca target=\"_blank\" href=\"http:\u002F\u002FGlenside,%20PA\"\u003EPA\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, 215\u002F572-2900, arcadia.edu.\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cspan class=\"yui-editorial-embed\"\u003E\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003Cimg title=\"&apos;Iolani (Photo: Jiang\u002FWikimedia Commons)\" alt=\"\" class=\"editorial \" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" align=\"right\" width=\"320\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Flo\u002Fapi\u002Fres\u002F1.2\u002FUpZ3pHgSZGmICwiWmMLPXg--\u002FYXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw\u002Fhttps:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fos\u002F153\u002F2012\u002F08\u002F16\u002F07-iolaniexterior-7262012-15534-horiz-large-jpeg_000142.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cp class=\"legend\"\u003E&apos;Iolani (Photo: Jiang\u002FWikimedia Commons)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003E&apos;Iolani Palace\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003EOther properties on this list may be bigger and more lavish, but the &apos;Iolani Palace has one thing above them all: legitimacy. America&apos;s only true palace&#x2014;as in, royalty resided here&#x2014;was built from 1879 to 1882 by King Kalakua and Queen Kapi&apos;olani. The goal was to enhance the prestige of modern Hawaii in a kind of Victorian-era keeping up with the Joneses. (The palace had electricity and a telephone even before the White House.) Stone-faced with plenty of koa wood inside, the two-floor American Florentine&#x2013;style building includes a throne room, grand hall, and private suites, including the upstairs room where the queen was imprisoned for five months following the 1895 coup. Today, concerted efforts are underway to find artifacts and furniture (like the king&apos;s ebony and gilt bedroom set) that were auctioned off by the post-coup Provisional Government. 364 South King St., \n\u003Ca target=\"_blank\" href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftravel.yahoo.com\u002Fp-travelguide-191501917-honolulu_vacations-i\"\u003EHonolulu, HI\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, 808\u002F522-0832, iolanipalace.org. Admission $12, guided tour $20.\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cspan class=\"yui-editorial-embed\"\u003E\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003Cimg title=\"Fonthill (Photo: 2daysphotos.com)\" alt=\"\" class=\"editorial \" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" align=\"right\" width=\"320\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Flo\u002Fapi\u002Fres\u002F1.2\u002FvDLLB7.rvpxPQX7L6ykNOw--\u002FYXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw\u002Fhttps:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fos\u002F153\u002F2012\u002F08\u002F16\u002F08-fonthillexterior-7262012-163622-horiz-large-jpeg_000142.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cp class=\"legend\"\u003EFonthill (Photo: 2daysphotos.com)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EFonthill Castle\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003ECelebrating its centennial in 2012, the former home of industrialist-turned-archaeologist Henry Mercer is an ode to artisanship: All 44 rooms (10 bathrooms, five bedrooms, and 200 windows), 32 stairwells, 18 fireplaces, and 21 chimneys are hewn from hand-mixed reinforced concrete in a mishmash of medieval, Gothic, and Byzantine styles. Thousands of handcrafted ceramic tiles were inset throughout, including Mercer&apos;s own Moravian-style tiles plus Persian, Chinese, Spanish, and Dutch productions he collected. Today, the 60-acre Bucks County estate serves as a museum to pre-industrial life, with 900 American and European prints at Fonthill and even more artifacts (like a whale boat and Conestoga wagon) in its sister building, the Mercer Museum, a fun house&#x2013;like six-story castle in its own right. East Court St. and Rt. 313, \n\u003Ca target=\"_blank\" href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftravel.yahoo.com\u002Fp-travelguide-478948-doylestown_vacations-i\"\u003EDoylestown, PA\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, 215\u002F348-9461, mercermuseum.org. Admission $12\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cspan class=\"yui-editorial-embed\"\u003E\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003Cimg title=\"Gillette Castle (Photo: Rootology\u002FWikimedia Commons)\" alt=\"\" class=\"editorial \" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" align=\"right\" width=\"320\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Flo\u002Fapi\u002Fres\u002F1.2\u002Feq9AEd4kkRJhZ9o1f8J4CQ--\u002FYXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw\u002Fhttps:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fos\u002F153\u002F2012\u002F08\u002F16\u002F09-giletteexterior-jpeg_000143.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cp class=\"legend\"\u003EGillette Castle (Photo: Rootology\u002FWikimedia Commons)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EGillette Castle\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003EIt&apos;s elementary: Get famous (and rich) by playing Sherlock Holmes on the stage; build your own Baskerville Hall. Pet project of campy eccentric William Hooker Gillette, the 24-room castle was completed in 1919 by a crew of 20 men over five years using the actor\u002Fplaywright&apos;s own drafts and designs. It&apos;s also the focal point of his 184-acre Seventh Sister estate, a forested bluff overlooking the Connecticut River. Outside, the local fieldstone reads like crumbling medieval; inside, the built-in couches, curious detailing, and inventive hand-carved southern white oak woodwork is all arts and crafts. As for cat images? There are 60. (Gillette had 17 feline friends.) Gillette Castle State Park, 67 River Rd., East Haddam, \n\u003Ca target=\"_blank\" href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftravel.yahoo.com\u002Fp-travelguide-191501900-connecticut_vacations-i\"\u003ECT\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, 860\u002F526-2336, ct.gov. Grounds open year-round; interior tours available Memorial Day to Columbus Day. Admission $6.\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cspan class=\"yui-editorial-embed\"\u003E\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003Cimg title=\"OHEKA Castle (Photo: Oheka Castle)\" alt=\"\" class=\"editorial \" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" align=\"right\" width=\"320\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Flo\u002Fapi\u002Fres\u002F1.2\u002Fy.gNt2ePLxIwkrervflR6Q--\u002FYXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw\u002Fhttps:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fos\u002F153\u002F2012\u002F08\u002F16\u002F10-ohekaexterior-7272012-12319-horiz-large-jpeg_000143.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cp class=\"legend\"\u003EOHEKA Castle (Photo: Oheka Castle)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EOHEKA Castle\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003ESecond behind Asheville&apos;s Biltmore as the largest private estate in the nation, OHEKA&#x2014;an acronym of Otto Herman Kahn, its millionaire financier original owner&#x2014;ended up abandoned in the late 1970s and sustained extensive damage from fires, vandals, and neglect. After a 20-year renovation, it&apos;s back in form and is now a 32-room luxury hotel. Think Downton Abbey just an hour from Manhattan (themed packages available), or for that matter, Citizen Kane (photos of it were used in the film). Originally set on 443 acres, massive tons of earth were moved to make the hilltop location of the 127-room, 109,000-square-foot manse the highest point in Long Island. The Olmsted Brothers planned the formal gardens, the Grand Staircase was inspired by Fontainebleau&apos;s famous exterior one, and 126 servants tended to the six-person family when they came for weekends and summers. The 1919 price tag: $11 million. That&apos;s $110 million in today&apos;s money. Sounds about right for a man whose likeness inspired Mr. Monopoly. 135 West Gate Dr., \n\u003Ca target=\"_blank\" href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftravel.yahoo.com\u002Fp-travelguide-4957035-huntington_ny_vacations-i\"\u003EHuntington, NY\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, 631\u002F659-1400, oheka.com. Admission $25. Double rooms from $395 per night.
